=300  \\$a[xii]-1040-[12] pages$bengraved frontispiece, title page in red and black ink, 28 insterted engraved plates
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aChristian devotional literature
=500  \\$aThe term "Erbauungsliteratur' (edification literature), first mentioned around the 14th century, originally describes popular writings with a religious motivation. Edification literature is not theological literature, as it does not pursue scientific discourses and has no dogmatic intentions. Rather, with the changes of the modern era, there was a focus on inwardness, which stood out through increased piety. It was a guide to a virtuous life that was intended to emotionally edify the mind. 
=500  \\$aJohannes Lassenius (1636-1692) was a German Lutheran theologian and devotional writer of the Baroque period.
=500  \\$abeautiful engravings, including one of a library (frontispiece)
=500  \\$aHeiligen Perlen-Schatzes in zwölf Vertheilungen was published in 3 volumes in Copenhagen 1688–89
=504  \\$ahttps://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Erbauungsliteratur
=590  \\$aZu Ausserbauung des Algemeinen Christenthums. In der Furcht des Herrn aufs Göttlichem Wort eingesamlet. Auch zu richtiger Verständnüss der heiligen Betrachtungen Uberal mit nöthigen Einbildern versehen

=500  \\$aWilhelmus Schortinghuis (1700-1750) was a Dutch Reformed clergyman. He is best known for his book 'Het Inninge Christendom' (1740) and the "vijf nieten" (the five nots): "ik wil niet, ik kan niet, ik weet niet, ik heb niet en ik deug niet" (I don't want to, I can't, I don't know, I don't have and I'm no good), with which he wanted to make clear. that a man could contribute nothing to his salvation. He is regarded as a representative of the late phase of the 'Nadere Reformatie', which is often referred to as Reformed Pietism.

=041  \\$afre
=100  \\$aSenault, Jean-François$d1599-1672$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q3165889$98453
=245  \\$aDe l'usage des passions
=260  \\$aParis$bJournel$c1660
=300  \\$alxxii-492 pages$bengraved frontispiece
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aOriginally published in 1641
=500  \\$aA book on the ‘usage’ of emotions by the French Augustinian preacher, Jean-François Senault. He approached the subject of the ‘passions’ from a variety of angles: their uses and dangers, how to moderate them and how a prince should use them. The treatise was often reprinted in different formats and translated into English, German, Italian and Spanish. The work is divided into two parts, the first of which deals with the passions in general and the last with each in particular.
=500  \\$aOf the nature of passions -- Of the disorder of passions -- Of the government of passions -- Of the commerce of passions with vertue and vice -- Of the power that passions have upon the will of man -- Of love and hatred -- Of desire and eschewing -- Of hope and despair -- Of audacity and fear -- Of choler or anger -- Of delight and sorrow.

=059  \\$av
=100  \\$aZuylen van Nijevelt, Willem van$d?-1543$4lyr$4col$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q2538170$98647
=245  \\$aSouter liedekens$bgemaeckt ter eeren Gods, op alle die Psalmen van David tot stichtinge, ende een gheestelijcke vermakinge van alle christen menschen
=260  \\$aUtrecht$bde Roy$c1598
=300  \\$a[364] pages$bmusic examples, engraved title page in red & black ink
=520  \\$aThe Souterliedekens (literal: Psalter-songs) is a Dutch metrical psalter, originally published in 1540 in Antwerp. The collection remained very popular throughout the century. The metrical rhyming psalms were probably arranged by Willem van Zuylen van Nijevelt (d. 1543), a nobleman from Utrecht, who created the melodies out of folk songs from the Low Countries (though some melodies have a German or French origin). This publication has great value, because the original publisher (Symon Cock) not only added the phrase 'sung to the tune of...', but also provided the actual music (melody) with the texts. Nowadays many of the folk song melodies that were known at that time can only be reconstructed because they have survived in the "Souterliedekens".
=534  \\$aOriginally published in 1540
=561  \\$aEx libris Seth Gaaikema (1939-2014), a Dutch cabaret artist, musical writer and translator.

=100  \\$aFleming, Paul$d1609-1640$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q77418$98650

=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aPaul Fleming (1609-1640), was a German physician and poet. Fleming is one of the writers now called "the Silesian poets" or "the Silesian school". As a lyricist he stands in the front rank of German poets.
=500  \\$aFleming wrote the hymn in nine stanzas "In allen meinen Taten" on the melody of "Innsbruck, ich muss dich lassen" by Heinrich Isaac, which is contained in several hymnals. Johann Sebastian Bach used the final stanza to close both cantatas Meine Seufzer, meine Tränen (BWV 13) and Sie werden euch in den Bann tun (BWV 44). The complete hymn is the base for Bach's chorale cantata In allen meinen Taten (BWV 97). Already in the 17th century another composer, David Pohle (1624–1695), had set twelve of Fleming's love-songs to music. Johannes Brahms set "Lass dich nur nichts bedauern" as Geistliches Lied, Op. 30.
=500  \\$acontains an engraved title page and a portrait of the author on the frontispiece
=534  \\$aTeutsche Poemata, published posthumously in 1642

=500  \\$aThe Histories, also known as The History of Herodotus, is considered the founding work of history in Western literature. Written in 430 BC in the Ionic dialect of classical Greek, 'The Histories' serves as a record of the ancient traditions, politics, geography, and clashes of various cultures that were known in Greece, Western Asia and Northern Africa at that time. The Histories were at some point divided into the nine books that appear in modern editions, conventionally named after the nine Muses.
=500  \\$aLorenzo Valla was an Italian Renaissance humanist, rhetorician, educator, scholar, and Catholic priest. He is best known for his historical-critical textual analysis. He is sometimes seen as a precursor of the reformation; Konrad Heresbach was a German Reformer, Calvinist, humanist and educator; Henri Estienne (1528-1598) was a French printer, philologist, Hellenist and humanist who published one of the most important lexica of the sixteenth century, the 'Thesaurus linguæ græcæ' (1572)

=500  \\$aOriginally published in 1551, the translations of 150 Psalms of David by Clement Marot (1496-1544) as completed by Theodore de Bèze (1519-1605, Calvin's successor as spiritual leader of the Republic of Geneva) were used almost exclusively by the Calvinists (Genevan Psalter). The psalter was the main medium of popular fervour among the Reformed. The Edict of Nantes forbade Reformed worship in towns where the King of France resided and the only town allowed around Paris was Charenton.

=500  \\$a'Iphigénie en Aulide'  is an opera in three acts by Christoph Willibald Gluck, the first work he wrote for the Paris stage. The libretto was based on Jean Racine's tragedy Iphigénie, itself based on the play Iphigenia in Aulis by Euripides. The choreography was by Gaétan Vestris. It was premiered on 19 April 1774 by the Paris Opéra in the second Salle du Palais-Royal and revived in a slightly revised version the following year.

=041  \\$adut
=245  \\$aWetten van het departement der muzyk, in de maatschappy, ter spreuke voerende: Felix Meritis
=260  \\$aAmsterdam$bUylenbroek$c1790
=300  \\$a31 pages$bengraved title page
=500  \\$aTitle page engraving (seated Apollo with lyre) after Jacques Kuyper (1761-1808), a Dutch printmaker, painter, draftsman, watercolourist, etcher, musician, and composer. Kuyper became a member of the Felix Meritis artist community.
=500  \\$astatutes of the music department within the Felix Meritis Society
=500  \\$aFelix Meritis ("Happy through Merit") is the name of an intellectual society for Music, Drawing, Physics, Commerce and Literature in Amsterdam, founded in 1776.  In 1788 the new building they built for themselves on the Keizersgracht in Amsterdam opened its doors. Felix Meritis’ oval concert hall was the main music hall in Amsterdam until late into the 19th century and enjoyed a great international reputation. Many famous musicians performed there, including Robert and Clara Schumann, Camille Saint-Saëns, Johannes Brahms and Julius Röntgen. The orchestra of Felix Meritis was regarded as the best of the Netherlands and accompanied many Dutch premieres, directed by conductors such as Johannes Bernardus van Bree. Thus, Beethoven’s Ninth Symphony and Berlioz’s Symphonie fantastique had their Dutch premiere in the concert hall of Felix Meritis. The small hall of the Concertgebouw is a replica of this concert hall.

=500  \\$aArranger Vuïet was a French journalist, novelist and composer, best known for opera. She was considered a child prodigy at age five and was presented to Queen Marie-Antoinette who  took her as an adopted daughter and saw that she received an education in the arts. Vuïet studied music under André Grétry, painting with Greuze and theater with Beaumarchais.

=100  \\$aChampein, Stanislas$d1753-1830$4cmp$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q3496656$98675
=245  \\$aOuverture de la Mélomanie.$cArrangée pour le clavecin ou le piano forte avec violon ad libitum
=260  \\$aParis$bBoyer$c1783
=300  \\$a10 pages$bPrinter's Signature stamp on title page
=500  \\$aArranger Charles Fodor was a Dutch composer and harpsichordist. He was the son of soldier Carolus Fodor (and later violinist) and Maria Elizabeth Messemaekcers, who came from a musical family. The brothers Joseph Fodor and Carolus Antonius Fodor also became musicians. Charles Fodor is the least known of the three brothers. He became a music teacher in Paris, made transcriptions of quartets by Pleyel and symphonies by Joseph Haydn. He himself wrote sonatas and variations (including Air de Tonnelier), but a symphony for large orchestra (Symphonie à grand orchester en re) by him is also known. There are also two concertos for harpsichord by him, one of which he performed in Amsterdam in December 1790. His works were mainly published in Paris and Amsterdam. He probably died in Paris in the last 10 years of the 18th century or early 19th century.
=500  \\$aLa Mélomanie. Opera Comique en un Acte, Mis en musique par M. S. Champein. Représenté pour la première fois sur le théâtre de l'Opéra comique national, le 23 janvier 1781

=500  \\$a Arranger Charles Fodor was a Dutch composer and harpsichordist. He was the son of soldier Carolus Fodor (and later violinist) and Maria Elizabeth Messemaekcers, who came from a musical family. The brothers Joseph Fodor and Carolus Antonius Fodor also became musicians. Charles Fodor is the least known of the three brothers. He became a music teacher in Paris, made transcriptions of quartets by Pleyel and symphonies by Joseph Haydn. He himself wrote sonatas and variations (including Air de Tonnelier), but a symphony for large orchestra (Symphonie à grand orchester en re) by him is also known. There are also two concertos for harpsichord by him, one of which he performed in Amsterdam in December 1790. His works were mainly published in Paris and Amsterdam. He probably died in Paris in the last 10 years of the 18th century or early 19th century.

=500  \\$aLa double épreuve, ou Colinette à la cour, is a comédie lyrique in three acts written by André Grétry in 1782 to a French libretto by Jean-Baptiste Lourdet de Santerre, based on Charles Simon Favart's Ninette à la cour. It was first performed on 1 January 1782 by the Académie Royale de Musique (Paris Opera) at the Théâtre de la Porte-Saint-Martin, and included choreography by Maximilien Gardel.

=500  \\$a'Alexis et Justine' a comédie lyrique mêlée d’ariettes in deux actes by Dezède on a libretto by Jaques-Marie Boutet de Monvel (1745-1812) premiered in Paris, Opéra-Comique, in 1783

=500  \\$aJohann Franz Metzger, born in Enkenbach in Landkreis Kaiserslautern, baptized December 26, 1729, was a German pianist and composer, from 1785 active in Paris. He was still alive in 1808 and probably died shortly afterwards. Metzger also composed cello sonatas, and dLa Bataille de Fleurus (tone painting for piano which describes the Battle of Fleurus in 1794), which was an important component of the well-known musical process in Uppsala in 1800, a notorious trial against seven academic citizens on the occasion of their "strike" as musicians in the Royal Academic Chapel at a party celebrating Gustav IV Adolf's coronation.

=100  \\$aGarth, John$d1721-1810$4cmp$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q2517501$95352
=245  \\$aA Second Sett of Six Sonatas for the Harpsichord, Piano Forte and Organ, with Accompanyments for two Violins and a Violoncello op. 4
=260  \\$aLondon$bWelcker$c17xx
=300  \\$a25 pages
=500  \\$aKeyboard part only
=500  \\$aGarth, English composer, organised for many decades a concert series, the Durham concerts, in alternate weeks to those organized by his friend Charles Avison in Newcastle, where Garth played the cello. Garth's fame spread and he taught music to leading families in the region, as well as giving organ recitals. Garth is chiefly remembered for his eight-volume edition with English text of The First Fifty Psalms Set to Music by Benedetto Marcello (1757–65), but he also composed a set of cello concertos (op. 1, 1760) and five sets of harpsichord sonatas (opp. 2, 4–7, 1768–82), among other works.

=500  \\$asong by a female composer, a member of the Ukrainian princely family Kotschoubey. Princess Elisabeth Vassilievna Kotschoubey (née Kotschoubey) (1821-1897) was a well known composer of both Russian and French popular songs in Russia and later in France. She was  married to her third cousin, Prince Leon Viktorovitch Kotschoubey (1810-1890) and they died childless. 
=500  \\$aEnrico Tamberlik (16 March 1820 – 13 March 1889) was an Italian tenor who sang to great acclaim at Europe and America's leading opera venues. He excelled in the heroic roles of the Italian and French repertories and was renowned for his powerful declamation and clarion high notes.
=500  \\$aText writer Larmande was a French state official (chef de bureau au Ministère des Finances), and amateur poet. Known for translating German songs, or rather for providing them with new, French poetry, e.g. in the series Échos d'Allemagne, together with Victor Wilder. His official signature (e.g. on his appointment as Chevalier de la légion d'honneur in 1881) always reads "Ad. Larmande", and his brother Alfred Larmande and sister-in-law Sophie Desargues were professional musicians.

=008  230228s1836\\\\|||||l||\||||\00|\0\fre\d
=041  \\$afre
=100  \\$aFontmichel, Hippolyte de$d1799-1874$4cmp$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q1298846$98722
=245  \\$aLe Chevalier de Canolle. Quadrille de contredanses suivi d'une valse, pour le piano, avec accomp. de violon, flûte ou flageolet, ad. libitum
=260  \\$aParis$bLemoine$c1836c
=300  \\$a7-[2] pages$bMusic-seller's stamp at foot of title page
=500  \\$aKeyboard part only
=500  \\$aPrinter's Plate No.1858.H.
=500  \\$aThe 5 numbers of the Quadrille are followed by a Galop;the score contains no 'Valse'.
=500  \\$aDe Fontmichel studied at the Conservatoire de Paris, and in 1822 he received the deuxième Second Grand Prix de Rome for the cantata Geneviève de Brabant. During his stay in Italy he composed two operas: Amadeo il Grande and I due Forzati. After the premiere in 1836 of the comic opera Le Chevalier de Canolle at the Opéra-Comique was a failure, de Fontmichel retired to Grasse, where he devoted himself to farming. Here he composed several opera choruses and an opera on the subject of Hamlet, as well as several romances. He also worked as organist at Grasse Cathedral and the Couvent de la Visitation and composed several religious works.
=500  \\$aHenry Lemoine was a French piano teacher, music publisher, and composer 
=500  \\$aPaper cover belongs to another work in the series of "Contredanses pour le Piano seul arranged and published by Lemoine, as title on the cover reads "à Madem.lle Louise de Golbéry. Par Henry Lemoine" and has printer's plate No 1966.H. "La Chatte..." is a one-act comic opera from 1858 by Jacques Offenbach, with a libretto by Eugène Scribe and Mélesville.

=500  \\$aNote on first mage: "Ce Pseaume est d'une grande Suavité. C'est le superius qui chante la Mélodie. =245  \\$aFeestmarsch ter gelegenheid des Zilveren Medaille. Juni 1892

=300  \\$a18 pages
=500  \\$aFrederik Gerardus Leistikow was the father of Louis H. F. Leistikow, musician & later conductor of a Dutch infantry regiment (wind band of the Netherlands Marine Corps/Marinierskapel der Koninklijke Marine, 1906-1940).
=520  \\$aSince the beginning of the 19th century, it has been customary in European courts to establish a decoration, usually a commemorative medal, to commemorate weddings, coronations and anniversaries. Such medals were usually awarded to guests, courtiers, servants and employees. The medal in question here was instituted in 1892 by Grand Duke Carl Alexander of Saxony. He and his Dutch wife Sophie celebrated their fiftieth wedding anniversary on 8 October. It was awarded in five different forms, including a silver one.

=500  \\$a'L'amor contrastato ossia La molinara' premiered in 1788 in Naples
=500  \\$aThe court oboist Franz Heinrich Ehrenfried worked for 44 years as a recognised musician in his field in the service of the Elector of Mainz or, after its dissolution, in Aschaffenburg. In addition, he played his role as a performing musician in opera, concert life and church music. There are numerous prints of his arrangements, mainly of operas. They offered the middle classes music for reliving stage works, for making music at home and for teaching purposes. The preference for the flute in these prints corresponds to the demand of the time.

=100  \\$aPhilidor, François-André Danican$d1726-1795$4cmp$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q203229$918157
=245  \\$aTom Jones. Comédie lyrique en trois actes
=260  \\$aParis$bde la Chevardiere$c1766
=300  \\$a16-16-12-14-6-5-5-5 pages
=500  \\$aTom Jones is a comédie mêlée d'ariettes, a kind of opéra comique which first appeared at the Comédie-Italienne, Paris, on 27 February 1765. Its French libretto, by Poisenet & Davesne, is loosely based on the 1749 novel by Henry Fielding. The opera was initially a failure but Philidor had the libretto revised by Sedaine and this new version, first performed on 30 January 1766, proved one of the most popular opéras comiques of the late 18th century. It was produced in a number of other countries, and translated into German, Swedish and Russian. 
=500  \\$aComplete instrumental parts, no vocal parts.

=041  \\$adut
=059  \\$av pf
=100  \\$aVoormolen, Alexander$d1895-1980$4cmp$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q2281256$96188
=245  \\$aCecilia (Oud Nederlandsch)
=246  \1$aCecilia. Middeleeuwsch Lied
=260  \\$aNetherlands$c1922
=300  \\$a5 pages
=500  \\$aPrinted and manuscript (Autograph?) version of the same song
=500  \\$aperformer's notes and markings in pensil on the manuscript version
=500  \\$acomposition place and date marked on manuscript version "'s-Gravenhage 1922"
=500  \\$aThis love song "Ik zag Cecilia komen" about the shepherds Cecilia and Floriaan, dates back to the 17th century. The oldest entry is in the Album of Geesken ter Borch (1652), with the opening line "Siet het pluijm gevogelt". The famous line with Cecilia is only found in verse 2 of the 2nd strophe. It also appears as "Lied van Cecilia" in the 'Dordrecht Helikon, ofte De Groote Dubbele Hollandsche Nachtegael' (1719). The song has lived on in the oral tradition, perhaps partly due to the fact that it has been included in numerous collections of folk songs. The melody is vaguely found in the Ballo di Mantova (Dance from Mantua) attributed to the guitar virtuoso Francisco Corbetta (1615-1681) and in "Fuggi fuggi da questo cielo" by Giuseppino Cenci (Giuseppino di Roma).

=500  \\$aNancy van der Elst was a female composer who taught in Utrecht
=500  \\$atranslation of Paul Gerhardt's Advent song "Wie soll ich dich empfangen"
=500  \\$a"Valet will ich dir geben" is a Lutheran hymn written by Valerius Herberger in 1613. It is a Sterbelied (hymn for the dying). The text was published with two hymn tunes by Melchior Teschner, Zahn Nos. 5403 and 5404a, in 1615. The second of these melodies was used in compositions such as chorale preludes by Johann Sebastian Bach and Max Reger. Bach used single stanzas in vocal works, including his St John Passion.
=500  \\$a"Our God, Our Help in Ages Past" is a hymn by Isaac Watts in 1708 that paraphrases the 90th Psalm of the Book of Psalms. In 1738, John Wesley in his hymnal, Psalms and Hymns, changed the first line of the text from "Our God" to "O God". Both Watts' wording and Wesley's rewording remain in current use.

=500  \\$aJoseph Schad was a German composer and organist. He was a pupil of Louis Schmitt in Frankfurt and for a time was dedicated to giving organ concerts. He established himself as an organist in Morges (CH) , later became a professor at the Conservatory of Genevavand finally settled in Bordeaux where he died. He wrote a large number of fantasies, transcriptions, waltzes, masurques, etc., for piano, vocal melodies and the ballet Franizia.

=100  \\$aMendelssohn-Bartholdy, Felix$d1809-1847$4cmp$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q46096$94998
=245  \\$aOuverture, Scherzo, Notturno, Hochzeitsmarsch und Intermezzo aus der Musik zu Shakespeare's Sommernachtstraum. Componirt und für das Pianoforte arrangirt op. 61
=260  \\$aRotterdam$bVletter, de$c1844 or later
=300  \\$a40 pages
=500  \\$aKeyboard arrangement by the composer
=500  \\$aAt two separate times, Felix Mendelssohn composed music for William Shakespeare's play A Midsummer Night's Dream (in German Ein Sommernachtstraum). First in 1826, near the start of his career, he wrote a concert overture (Op. 21). Later, in 1842, only a few years before his death, he wrote incidental music (Op. 61) for a production of the play, into which he incorporated the existing overture. The incidental music includes the famous "Wedding March". 
=500  \\$aIn 1844 Mendelssohn arranged three movements for piano solo (Scherzo, Nocturne, Wedding March), which received their first recording by Roberto Prosseda in 2005. Slightly better known is the composer's own arrangement, also made in 1844, of five movements for piano duet (Overture, Scherzo, Intermezzo, Nocturne, Wedding March).

=100  \\$aHöckh, Carl$d1707-1773$4cmp$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q16859335$98775
=245  \\$aSieben Parthien von zweyen Violinen und Baß
=260  \\$aBerlin$bWinter$c1761
=300  \\$a8-8-8 pages$bengraved cover page $c35x23 cm
=500  \\$aThree parts (violino primo, violino secondo, cembalo) in an engraved paper envelope 
=500  \\$aThe term parthia or partita is by no means to be understood as an unambiguous genre designation; rather, it is used as a kind of collective term. In the present works, it is applied to a trio sonata type with two equal violins and basso continuo, which in turn can be interpreted as a transitional stage to the sonata forms of the burgeoning genres of string trio, piano trio and string quartet.
=500  \\$aHöckh, who was music director at Zerbst on the recommendation of Benda, is considered "one of the founders of the German school of violin playing". He wrote extensively and idiomatically for the instrument, incorporating more advanced techniques than most of his contemporaries. His works include eleven symphonies, seventeen violin concertos, seven partitas, twenty-seven violin sonatas, and thirty-four capricetti.
=500  \\$aEdited by Phillip Schmidt, Ortus Musikverlag, om97
=500  \\$aWhat is curious about the parthias is their unusual number for the 18th century. The Seven Parthias in A, B, C, D, e, F, g are inscribed with Italian tempo markings and are mainly structured in their movement sequence like the modern trio sonata according to the principle fast - slow - fast. Exceptions are the IIIrd Parthia, in which the first movement is heard again after the second, and the IVth Parthia, whose structure is four movements. The final movement here is a tempo di minuetto. Some of the middle movements are in the key of the subdominant, the fourth in the key of the Variant, the sixth in the key of the dominant and the last in the key of the mediant.

=041  \\$aita
=100  \\$aBallabeni, Pietro Antonio$dfl. 1735$4aut$98799
=245  \\$a[Letter to Padre Giovanni Battista Martini?]
=260  \\$as.l.$c1735
=300  \\$a3 pages
=500  \\$aDated 2 April 1735 and sent from Prato, this letter is certainly addressed to Padre Martini, the Maestro di Capella of S. Francesco in Bologna, although the recipient's name has been removed from the address. The otherwise untraceable Frate Ballabeni informs Martini of the death of the Maestro di Capella [Giovanni Francesco] Beccatelli (1679-1735), which had occurred the day before, and asks him to forward this to the Maestro di Capella Bononcini. He offers his correspondent the deceased's musical manuscripts and his extensive library for sale. In the postscript Ballabeni asks the addressee to spread the word in Bologna that the position of Maestro di Capella in Prato is to be filled and that the salary for this position is 140 scudi. Mentioned in the letter, furthermore, are Giovanni Bononcini (long linked to Bologna, where has was a member of the Accademia Filarmonica) and Sicinio Pepoli (a Bolognese count who corresponded with Farinelli, among others).

=100  \\$aTasso, Torquato$d1544-1595$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q168962$94904
=245  \\$aL'Aminte
=260  \\$aThe Hague$bDyk, van$c1681
=300  \\$a[xii]186 pages$bbound in marbled cardboard, manuscript title vignet on spine, inserted illustrations, frontispiece engraving
=500  \\$aOriginally published in 1580
=500  \\$abilingual edition italian-french "Aminta, Comedia / Aminte, Comedie"
=500  \\$aAminta is a play written by Torquato Tasso in 1573, represented during a garden party at the court of Ferrara. Both the actors and the public were noble persons living at the Court, who could understand subtle allusions the poet made to that style of life, in contrast with the life of shepherds, represented in an idyllic way. The text is written in hendecasyllabic and septenary verses; it is divided into five acts. The play has a pastoral theme, and is set in the time of Alexander the Great. The characters are shepherds and nymphs.The story is about Aminta's love for the beautiful nymph Silvia, who does not return his attentions and prefers hunting. She risks rape at the hands of a Satyr but Aminta saves her; however, again she flees from him. Aminta, finding her blood-stained veil, attempts to kill himself. Now Silvia is remorseful, comes back to cry over Aminta's body who is still alive, and the two can happily marry, following the advice that older and wiser friends had been giving them.

=100  \\$aBaranius, August Wilhelm$4aut$98829
=245  \\$aVersuch einer Biographie der Frau Gräfin von Lichtenau
=260  \\$aZurich$aLindau$a[Leipzig]$bs.n.$c1800 [1798]
=300  \\$a[x]-132 pages
=500  \\$aWilhelmine, Gräfin von Lichtenau, born as Wilhelmine En(c)ke, also spelled Encke (1753-1820), was the official mistress of King Frederick William II of Prussia from 1769 until 1797 and was elevated by him into the nobility. She is regarded as politically active and influential in the policy of Prussia during his reign.
=500  \\$aAccording to Waltraud Maierhofer, Wilhelmine was often the subject of satire during her lifetime. This publication, actually published in Leipzig in 1798, seems to be "more a satire against enlightenment ideas than a biography". The author's name, August Wilhelm Baranius, might even be a pseudonym; Waltraud Maierhofer suggests the opera singer Henrietta Baranius (1768-1853). (Source: “Wilhelmine Encke-Ritz-Lichtenau: Writing and Reading the life of a Prussian Royal Mistress." Biography 27, no. 3 (2004): 575–96.)

=100  \\$aAnonymous$4lbt$94790
=245  \\$aLetra a la tonadilla a doce, intitulada: La Plaza de Palacio de Barcelona
=260  \\$aBarcelona$bCampins$c1774
=300  \\$a13-[2] pages$bmodern white vellum binding
=500  \\$aTonadilla was a Spanish musical song form of theatrical origin; not danced. The genre was a type of short, satirical musical comedy popular in 18th-century Spain, and later in Cuba and other Spanish colonial countries. It originated as a song type, then dialogue for characters was written into the tonadilla, and it expanded into a miniature opera lasting from 10 to 20 minutes. It drew its personages from everyday life and included popular and folk music and dance, and vernacular language. The tonadilla also influenced the development of the zarzuela, the characteristic form of Spanish musical drama or comedy. 
=500  \\$aOne of the works Valledor wrote when he was the first musician of the Barcelona Theatre
=500  \\$aNote from the antiquarian Kraus, NY "The only edition of this little tonadilla, a theatrical form which reached its apogee in the eighteenth century in the urban theatre. ... There is a list of tonadillas available from the same printer at the end of the volume...."

=500  \\$aMarmontel is a French encyclopaedist, historian, storyteller, novelist, grammarian, poet, playwright and philosopher. He was close to Voltaire in his views and was an opponent of Rousseau. Marmontel enjoyed fame throughout Europe thanks to the French court where he gained the patronage of the influential "maîtresse en titre" Madame de Pompadour in 1758, but his work was highly controversial.

=500  \\$aChristian Friedrich Franckenstein (1621-1679) was a German teacher, classical philologist and historian.
=500  \\$aChristina (1626-1689) was a member of the House of Vasa, and the Queen of Sweden in her own right from 1632 until her abdication in 1654. The Swedish queen is remembered as one of the most learned women of the 17th century. She was fond of books, manuscripts, paintings, and sculptures. With her interest in religion, philosophy, mathematics, and alchemy, she attracted many scientists to Stockholm, wanting the city to become the "Athens of the North". The Peace of Westphalia allowed her to establish an academy or university when and wherever she wanted.
=534  \\$aOriginally published in 1708
=590  \\$aSedert haar geboorte tot op des zelfs dood. Waar in naaukeurig, en na waarheit haar geheele manier van regeering, secreete handelingen, raadspleegingen, heldendaaden, minneryen enz. verhandeld werd. Door een van haar Staatsbedienden van tijd tot tijd versamelt, in 't Italiaansch beschreeven, nu in het Nederduitsch gebragt, met nodige figuuren en registers verrijkt.

=041  \\$aeng
=100  \\$aSwift, Jonathan$d1667-1745$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q41166$97332
=245  \\$aA Tale of a Tub
=250  \\$a9th ed.
=260  \\$aLondon$bBathurst$c1739
=300  \\$a[xxiv]-220 pages$b7 plates inserted, engraved frontispiece
=500  \\$aA 'Tale of a Tub' (see also 11A18 for the French translation) was first published by the Irish clergyman and novelist Jonathan Swift in 1704; it is the first and perhaps most difficult of all his satires. The title is thought to refer to a dissenting priest’s pulpit, and the work is a biting parody on the religious extravagances that Swift perceived among the clergy at the start of the 18th century. The narrative is written using a complex though playful technique of interlinking stories concerning the lives of three brothers, each representing one of the main branches of western Christianity. The edition is particularly noteworthy for the woodcut illustrations that punctuate the text. For example, there is a striking image of a priest reprimanding the congregation down below, with a gallows and theatre shown in the background. The frontispiece also illustrates a whale distracted by a barrel thrown overboard by sailors: an allegory, perhaps, of how the text was designed to draw the attention of political and religious dissenters away from the affairs of the ‘ship’ of state.
=534  \\$aOriginally published in 1704
=590  \\$aWritten for the Universal Improvement of Mankind. To which is added, an Account of a Battle between the Antient and Modern Books in St. James's Library. (...) With the Author's Apology. And Explanatory Notes by W.W.--tt--n, B.D. and Others.

=245  \\$aQuestions sur les mathématiques en général

=500  \\$aoriginates from a Benectine monastery school ?
=500  \\$aEx libris "Dom Antoine Jourdez", the last Benedictine monk of Toul, who wrote a handwritten document, entitled Description of the organ, 1811 and 1813. Attached to this 422-page manuscript is a 47-page Supplement, written in 1882, by Joseph Oury, organist of Toul Cathedral. The organ of the former Saint-Étienne Cathedral of Toul (Meurthe-et-Moselle) seemed to have passed through the Revolution without incident. When the church reopened, the last of the Benedictine monks of Saint-Mansuy, Dom Antoine Jourdez, had the organ restored and assumed the position of organist until September 30, 1828.

=100  \\$aSweerts, Cornelis$d1669-1742$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q2311859$98901

=250  \\$a1st ed.
=260  \\$aAmsterdam$bStrander$c1704
=300  \\$a[xii]-128-[4] pages$billustrations
=500  \\$aCornelis Sweerts (1669-1749) was a poet, songwriter, playwright and bookseller. His 'Inleiding tot de zang- en speelkunst' describes musical life in Amsterdam at the end of the 17th century. In it, he makes a plea for writing in the Dutch language and composing on Dutch texts (in reaction to French and Italian).
=500  \\$aTogether with Abraham Alewijn he is considered to be among the two most important songwriters of his time. They published a total of eight songbooks, which were reprinted many times. Their song texts were set to music mainly by the composers David Petersen, Nicolaas Ferdinand le Grand, Hendrik Anders and Servaes de Koninck.

=500  \\$aThe 'Encyclopédie ou Dictionnaire universel raisonné des connaissances humaines', ed. by Fortunato Bartolomeo De Felice, appeared between 1770 and 1780 in Yverdon; it was strongly anti-religious.
=500  \\$aDe Felice, an Italian nobleman, was a famed author, philosopher, scientist, and is said to have been one of the most important publishers of the 18th century. He is considered a pioneer of education in Switzerland, and a formative contributor to the European Enlightenment.
=500  \\$aIn an accompanying letter from Mr. Boogaarts to Ton Koopman, it is suggested that the copy of the Yverdon article from 1770 was made by Frans C. Smit (1800-1876) around c. 1825, and that this manuscript was part of the inheritance of Arie Bouman (Dutch barritone and organist 1911-1999), whose personal archives are preserved in the Utrecht Organ Archive iof the Utrecht University Library. As an organ consultant, Bouman left his mark on the Dutch organ scene for decades.

=041  \\$ager
=100  1\$aHaller, Albrecht von$d1708-1777$4edt$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q123225$98927
=245  \\$aGöttingische Zeitungen von gelehrten Sachen auf das Jahr MDCCLI$nnos. 1-7, 11-114, 117-124, 127-128
=260  \\$aGöttingen$bSchmid$c1751
=300  \\$a[vi]-1296-[40] pages
=500  \\$aThe Göttingische Gelehrten Anzeigen is considered as the oldest scholarly journal still published in the German-speaking world. In this specialised journal, scholars critically review contemporary scientific works. The first volume was published in 1739 under the title Göttingische Zeitung(en) von gelehrten Sachen, from 1747 under the direction of the physician Albrecht von Haller. From 1753, the journal was published by the Göttingen Academy of Sciences and Humanities, which was founded in 1751, and was called Göttingische Anzeigen von gelehrten Sachen until 1801. The current title was introduced in 1802; since then the journal has been published by Vandenhoeck & Ruprecht, with the exception of the years 1896 to 1935, when it was published by the Berlin publishing house Weidmann. There were only interruptions between 1944 and 1953, as well as in 1960 and 1961.

=500  \\$aCaptivi is a Latin play by the early Roman playwright Titus Maccius Plautus, written circa 200 BCE. The title has been translated as The Captives or The Prisoners, and the plot focuses on slavery and prisoners of war. Although the play contains much broad humor, it is a relatively serious treatment of significant themes compared to most of Plautus’ other comedies.

=500  \\$aFrançoise de Graffigny (1695-1758), better known as Madame de Graffigny, was a French novelist, playwright and salon hostess.
=500  \\$aLetters from a Peruvian Woman is a 1747 epistolary novel. It tells the story of Zilia, a young Incan princess, who is abducted from the Temple of the Sun by the Spanish during the Spanish conquest of the Inca Empire. In a series of letters to her fiancé Aza, who is also the Sapa Inca, Zilia tells the story of her capture, her rescue by French sailors, her befriending of the captain Déterville and her introduction to French society.

=041  \\$afre
=100  \\$aGrignion de Montfort, Louis-Marie$d1673-1716$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q88927$4aut$98943
=245  \\$aCantiques des missions
=260  \\$aPoitiers$bFaulcon$c1779
=300  \\$a258-[3] pages$bleather bound, embossed gilded spine
=500  \\$aLouis-Marie Grignion de Montfort was a French Catholic priest known for his preaching and his influence on Mariology. He was made a missionary apostolic by Pope Clement XI. Montfort wrote a number of books which went on to become classic Catholic titles and influenced several popes.
=500  \\$aWhile Montfort is best known for his spiritual writings, he was also a poet and during his missions managed to compose more than 20,000 verses of hymns. His hymns and canticles were, for the most part, meant to be sung in village churches and in the homes of the poor. Based on the analysis of Bishop Hendrik Frehen of the Company of Mary, Montfortian hymns fall into two major categories: "inspired" and "didactic." The inspired canticles flow spontaneously, on the occasion of a pilgrimage to a Marian shrine, or on the occasion of a joyful celebration. The didactic hymns took more effort and time to compose, and focus on instructional and informative qualities: they teach the audience through the use of a moral and a theme. After Montfort's death, the Company of Mary (which continued his work of preaching parish renewals) made great use of his hymns and used them as instruments of evangelization.

=300  \\$a11 pages
=500  \\$aDescription of Pascal Taskin's 'forté-piano en forme de clavecin' and its mechanism
=500  \\$aAbove the text is written: "de la part de Blanchet, Elêve et successeur de P. Taskin"; Below the text is printed: "Au Louvre, le 13 décembre 1788. Signés, Vandermonde, Hauy, Baron Dietrick". That would probably be Alexandre-Théophile Vandermonde, René Just Haüy, and Baron Philippe-Frédéric de Dietrich, all members of the Academie royale des Sciences at the time.  

=520  \\$aBlanchet was a pupil of Taskin, but Taskin was also pupil of Blanchet. François-Étienne Blanchet II (c. 1730-1766) was François-Étienne Blanchet I's son and like him became a harpsichord maker, learning from his father. Pascal Taskin became his apprentice and took over his workshop after his early death. Armand-François-Nicolas Blanchet (1763-1818) was the son of François-Étienne Blanchet II and brought up and trained by Pascal Taskin after his father's early death.

=100  \\$aBraunschweig-Lüneburg, Sophie Elisabeth von$d1613-1676$4cmp$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q448131$98975
=245  \\$aChrist Fürstliches Davids-Harpfen-Spiel
=260  \\$aNuremberg$bGerhard$c1667
=300  \\$a[xxx]-265-[5] pages
=500  \\$aHyms and devotional arias
=500  \\$aSophie Elisabeth von Braunschweig-Lüneburg was a German poet, composer and impressario, and by marriage Duchess of Brunswick-Lüneburg. Most of Elisabeth Sophie 's compositions are hymns or devotional arias. Some of these were published in 1651 and 1667. The one printed in 1651, Vinetum evangelicum, Evangelischer Weinberg, is believed to have been the first music published by a woman in Germany. Her stephson Anton Ulrich was a patron of the arts, a writer, an art collector and one of the main proponents of enlightened absolutism among the Brunswick dukes.

=500  \\$a1645-1666 : Augustin Ier Le Scellier was abbot of the Prémontré Abbey , the mother house of the Premonstratensian Order, located at Prémontré about twelve miles west of Laon, département of Aisne, France. The Order of Canons Regular of Prémontré (Latin: Candidus et Canonicus Ordo Praemonstratensis), also known as the Norbertines is a religious order of canons regular of the Catholic Church founded in Prémontré near Laon in 1120 by Norbert of Xanten, who later became Archbishop of Magdeburg. Premonstratensians are designated by O.Praem. (Ordo Praemonstratensis) following their name.

=520  \\$aDespite his modest origins, Angelo Medori's talent induced his father to enroll him at the Liceo musica di Bologna where he graduated with honors in composition in 1866. The same year he returned to Viterbo where he was elected choirmaster of the cathedral. She also held the position of director of the municipal band for sixteen years and that of teacher in the municipal music school. In 1878 he became an honorary member of the Academy of Santa Cecilia. He composed numerous pieces of music and in 1887 he ventured into melodrama with the four-act opera 'La Galiana', legendary heroine from Viterbo, represented at the Teatro Unione on 8 September 1887.

=500  \\$aCollection of arias for soprano in different hands. Some arias have the name [Mlle Monville] on top. Could this be a collection for the soprano Mlle Monville (?-1768), the creator of Œnone, Phèdre's confidante in Rameau's 'Hippolyte et Aricie' in 1733? She was equally casted in 'Achille et Deidamie' by Campra, 'Scanderberg' by Francœur & Rebel, 'Les Voyages de l'Amour' by Boismortier and 'Le Triomphe de l'Harmonie' by Grenet.
=500  \\$aThe aria in E Major "So che fedele" could derive from Sacchini's 'Creso' (Naples, 1765); while the aria in E-flat Major "Pavento ah giusti Dei" could derive from Sacchini's 'Montezuma' (London, 1775)

=500  \\$aSix pages of organ music in different hands, from the second half of the eighteenth century, partly copies, partly autographs, including a fragment by John Stanley and four organ pieces (Voluntary, Präludium, Fuge ect) by an anonymous composer. In addition, there an organ intavolation of a four-part piece by Thomas Tallis (dixit the antiquarian).
=500  \\$aPage 3 is part of Stanley's Voluntaries for the Organ or Harpsichord op. 6 no. 2 (print see 03J49)
